text:
I make this ALL the time. Its the best slow cooker recipe ever! The only thing I change is I use chicken broth instead of white wine, and I use regular cream of mushroom soup- it has a better flavor than the golden mushroom soup. I always serve over angel hair pasta with a nice crusty bread to soak up the fabulous sauce. This is one of my all time favorite recipes!! I cook on high for 3-4 hours, OR on low for 6-8 hours.

text:
great but easier version is: pan fry sliced onion & mushrooms in butter, then add chicken sprinkled with a lot of italian spices & fresh ground pepper, brown both sides.  Add 2 cans regular mushroom soup, the chive & onion cream cheese (if you have only regular cream cheese use that) a few TB sour cream, heat through, add wine but it's better with about 1/3 cup sherry. Serve with cut-up fresh chives& parsley. Great with mashed potatoes or served on heated pastry shells.We like a lot of sauce, so you can play around by adding or deleting.  Only takes about 20 min from start to finish and it's unbelievably great.

text:
Great taste, but way too salty. I like salt, but this dish is for salt addicts. I would definitely make again but cut the amount of Italian dressing pack to half or a quarter of packet. 

Update: 12/4
I made this recipe again today, the meal came out perfect. Here is what I changed to cut down high salt taste.

2 tbsp butter
1/2 of single packet (.7 oz) dry Italian dressing 
1 8oz  brick of cream cheese (chive cream cheese is too salty when mixed with other ingredients)
1 tbsp of chive seasoning
1 can of condensed golden mushroom soup
1/2 cup dry white wine
8 skinless boneless chicken tenderloins

-follow same basic cooking directions in recipe

I served this with a half of a box of mini penne noodles. I put 2 tabs of butter on noodles and pinch of salt & teaspoon of oregano on noodles. When you are ready to eat, just top noodles with delicious chicken & sauce.

text:
My boyfriend and I really liked this recipe.  I made it with 98% fat free condensed mushroom soup and 1/3 less fat chive and onion cream cheese, plus changed the butter to use a lower fat spreadable butter made with olive oil.  The only cooking wine I had was a dry white with lemon, so I used that.  I don't like reviews that say they changed every ingredient in the recipe and that made it 5 stars, so while I did make some changes, I tried to stick to as true to the recipe as possible, just using lower fat ingredients.  I will definitely make this again.  To add a vegetable to the dish, I added a 16oz bag of frozen broccoli after the dish had cooked for 3 hours.  We served it over pasta, and my boyfriend went back for seconds (he doesn't usually eat much!).

text:
This was a last minute dinner choice as our dinner guests cancelled, noone wanted lasagna and I'm sick as a dog. I changed the recipe just a bit, to add more flavor. I sauteed some sliced onion, minced garlic and 4 ounces sliced baby bella mushrooms in the butter (I needed to add a little more butter) before adding in the other ingredients. Because I didn't have chive and onion cream cheese, I used the reduced fat cream cheese I had on hand and added in a teaspoon of onion powder and a couple tablespoons of fresh chopped chives. We thought this was very good, even my husband who can be kind of iffy with cream "gravy" type dinners. No leftovers. I served this with fluffy brown rice and roasted broccoli and cauliflower. Very budget friendly and quite bendable to make it more personal.

text:
This is a favorite of mine for the slower cooker.  However, I've added a few things to it.  Once you have the mixture cooked in the saucepan and ready to add to the slow cooker, try adding in quartered artichoke hearts (I use one can), drained diced tomatoes (1 can) and 1/2 to 1 onion (how much do you like onions?).  Then at the end of cooking I shred/slice the chicken and mix throughout the sauce.  Serve over bow-tie pasta with fresh parmesan on top.  So good!  If it is too thick I toss in a bit of vegetable or chicken broth as well.

text:
How nice to be surprised. I haven't always been happy with crock pot meals but this is a recipe that I will keep and make again for sure. Rather than cut back on salt (a few reviewers said "too salty") I used unsalted butter and paid attention to how much salt there was already built in the called for ingredients that I cannot control - the soup for example. I'm a Kosher salt fan as I find the flavour is less harsh and more pleasing even when using less. As a personal preference I used half white wine and half chicken broth. I was unsure if 4 hours on low would be long enough so I began at high for about an hour then turned to low for the remaining time. The chicken was very tender and the sauce smooth. I served it over basmati rice with a broccoli side. Delicious! 
The following night I made egg noodles serving  them with the remaining sauce. 
Add economical as another bonus. Thanks so much for posting.

Yummy! I made a few minor changes. I sauteed fresh mushrooms and lots of garlic in the butter before adding the other ingredients. text:
This is a lovely recipe which I made following several reviewers' suggestions and a few of my own alterations according to my available ingredients and preferences. The family really enjoyed it! I used 4 large chicken breasts (each cut in 3) and placed on bottom of slow cooker with 1/4 c of broth. I sauted a large onion before adding cream of broccoli soup (it's what I had!) and plain light cream cheese. I omitted the Italian powder in favour of 1T each of dried parsley, oregano and chives, and 1/2 T basil. I added 1/2 c chicken broth instead of wine  and mixed thouroughly before pouring over the chicken. 
It was perfect after cooking it on high for 3 hours. A few minutes before serving, I added 2 chopped green onions. We had it over spaghetti noodles with peas. Next time I may try it with angel hair pasta or spaghetti squash. Yum!

text:
For cooks and reviewers who say it is bland .  The recipe doesn't have  any flavours or aromatics to give it a wow. One has to do that themselves. I most  always  add ,onion,garlic and herbs to flavour my food dishes.
I made this and it was great. I had mushrooms i needed to use up and 8 chicken thighs. I use what i have on hand . I very seldom run out and buy specifically   for a recipe. You can always adapt and use what you have on hand. 
I sauted the mushrooms in butter,garlic,onion , and  a pinch of red chili peppers.
 I added  plain cream cheese  because that is what i had, cream of chicken soup, a  tbsp of chicken bouillon, 1/2 cup of wine,some herbs, sage leaves and thyme leaves, parsley , because i have in my garden,which go nice with both mushrooms and chicken. 
I  put a sprinkle of salt and pepper on the chicken  thighs and topped with the creamy soupy mushroom mixture.
I cooked on high 3 hrs then the last hr or so  on low.
It was delicious served over  buttered,parsley eggs noodles  with a side of garlic sauteed broccoli.
.If you want flavour cooks you have to add it and yes you will have tweaked the recipe,but all recipes are open to  tweaking, if you are an adventurous  cook.
 Don't be afraid to add aromatics to bring out flavour..This is a  good base recipe for just that or enjoy as is.

text:
I read most of the reviews, and I thought I'd play with this recipe.  So, here's what I did...
First of all, I wasn't in a time crunch this time so I didn't dump and run (haha).
I turned my slow cooker on HI added the butter and let it melt. Then, I added the chicken breasts with rib meat.  I think a dark piece or two would be a good addition, and will do it next time. I sprinkled each side with Chicken Tickler, you can find it online, and/or lemon pepper, and 1/2 packet of Italian seasoning.  I would suggest some kind of all purpose seasoning with minimal to no salt added. while I let one side with seasoning get some heat, 20 min. I made the sauce. I used LOW SODIUM cream of chicken AND regular Golden mushroom, and LOW SODIUM chicken broth.  I believe regular cream of mushroom makes it bland. In a saucepan, I whisked the golden mushroom, Low sodium cream of chicken, 4-6 oz of the cream cheese and NOT the whole 8 oz, MUST use the 1/2 cup of wine, and 1/2 cup LOW SODIUM Chicken broth. Whisk gently, let get hot.
Flip your chkn in crockpot, add another splash of wine, a tablespoon of SUGAR and then add the sauce.  I used HI for 41/2 hours and LOW for an hour or two.  It was absolute perfection!  House smelled divine. Use rice.
If you think it's too salty, you can add more sugar.
Bon appetite!

text:
I've always been very picky about slow cooker meals. I find that some meals can easily be thrown in and come out very good while other meals should remain cooked on the stove top. I substituted the wine for chicken broth, used cream of mushroom instead of golden and only used half of the salad dressing packet. I seasoned the chicken breast with herbs and red pepper only since the dressing, cream of mushroom and cream cheese have enough salt in them in my opinion. The smell was heavenly while it cooked and I put it over angel hair pasta once is was done. I can easily say that it was the best meal that ever came out of the slow cooker. Very easy and something that I never would have thought would be so delicious thrown all together. Thank you for sharing!

I made this one day when I was in a crunch for time later in the day and needed dinner alredy taken care of. I made it for my family of six: a very picky husband, and four picky children ages 10-13. I didn't have any wine in the fridge, but I DID have a 12 oz. can of beer, so I used that instead. IT WAS INCREDIBLE!!! I will always make this with beer from now on. I WOULD suggest spending the time to really melt the cream cheese and make sure it's blended in well before adding everything to the crock pot. I didn't, and there were random chuncks of cream cheese still floating in the mix at the end. I served this over plain rice and doubled up on the liquid so I could pour it over the chicken on the bed of rice. All of my picky eaters cleaned their plates and went back for seconds. There were no leftovers this night. My husband is begging me to make it again.

text:
This is excellent. It is very much like the "Angel Chicken Pasta" recipe, which we love! I do like that this is a slow-cooker version. It is easier this way. The Angel Chicken recipe uses half of the cream cheese listed for this version. I prefer less cream cheese, and I used only half of the tub. In my opinion, the wine and use of Golden Mushroom soup, really make the sauce. Using Cream of Mushroom completely changes the recipe. I also use 3 tbsp of butter, a small can of mushrooms (we love mushrooms), and a quarter cup of chicken broth. Although, this recipe is very good just as written. These are just my personal taste preferences, after making this recipe MANY times. DELICIOUS!

I'm giving this a three not because it didn't taste good, but because a recipe that has this many calories should be one of the best things you've ever put in your mouth!  I knew when making it that this was not a low calorie dinner by any means.  But, as I was making it I realized that just an 8 oz container of chive/onion cream cheese is 720 calories!  Not to mention the butter and mushroom soup.  It is not a bad recipe though.  Definitely not worthy of 5 stars, but worthy of 4 if you cut down the calories by using other ingredients (if that's even possible).  I added fresh mushrooms to this, and served it over asparagus.  Rice was my first choice, but wasn't eating any more calories!  I think it needed something else, as it provided a one-note soupy flavor.  Maybe putting chives on top would have balanced out the taste a bit, and added a little crunch.

I volunteered to bring this dish to a pre-Thanksgiving lunch and found I lost the recipe.  Total panic.  Finally found it.  I tweak it a bit.  Use low fat cream cheese, lose the butter and use mushroom soup.  100 years ago when I had my first crockpot, I had a recipe for chicken with sour cream and tarragon so I add a dollop of sour cream and tarragon to taste.  Somewhere along the line, I add a good splash of white wine.  This time, no one will want a whole chicken breast so I intend to cut the chicken into bite size pieces and brown them lightly with a sprinkling of garlic salt.  I love this recipe and have been known to stand over the crock pot slurping up the sauce.  I personally think it's best over fresh linguine topped with fresh chives.

Husband was totally impressed! This had to be one of the easiest and the most flavorful chicken dishes I've ever made! It also kept the chicken moist and the mixture doesn't burn. Same as Angel Chicken but either way, it's terrific!! The wine gives the flavor some nice zip...but occasionally we have to sub chicken broth if out of white cooking wine, and the flavor is almost identical. I also add a soup can of milk to help keep the soup mixture from getting too thick and overcooking while it is in the crockpot. I originally thought it was strange to cook the mixture in a pan before putting it in the crock pot, but after doing it I could see why with using cream cheese (even when softened). Good recipe with good instructions. Love, love, love it!

text:
Overall, this dish had potential. My boyfriend and I both rated it a 6.5/10. I made this recipe after reading all the reviews and taking into consideration all the suggestions/alterations. Because reviews were saying it was too salty I only used 1/2 of the dry italian mix, and instead of wine (because I didn't have wine in the house - this never happens) I used 1/4c chicken broth and 1/4c water. This reduced the saltiness of the meal, but it still wasn't "the best chicken recipe ever". I cooked it for 4.5 hours, adding sliced mushrooms after 4 hours, and served it with basmati rice and steamed broccoli. Saved the chicken for leftovers. May make again with more adjustments.

This is incredible!!  I put sea salt on the chicken breasts and let them "marinate" while I was mixing everything together for the sauce (I always salt chicken before crock-pot cooking, it really helps bring out the flavor.)  I did use about 1 cup (instead of 1/2 c) of white wine to make more "juice" for the dish.  I used cream of mushroom soup b/c I didn't have the other on hand. I didn't have tomatoes so I couldn't do this, but I'll bet it would taste (and look) amazing!

text:
I used the recipe but doubled it because we chose to make portobello mushroom ravioli to go with the chicken rather than rice and it was a good decision with this phenominal sauce. What we changed in the recipe were substitutions. I didn't have enough of the cream cheese so I added 8 oz of sour cream and it turned out wonderful. Depending on how thick your chicken breasts are check them at 3 to 3 1/2 hours to see if they need to be turned or moved. And  chicken, with that particular sauce... really good with pasta. My family are fans of this and they don't care for mushroom soup. For the soup I used 1 10 1/2 oz can Cream of Mushroom with Garlic and 1 10 1/2 oz can Cream of Cremini & Shitake Mushroom soup. (Campbells). I added 3 cloves of fresh crushed garlic. Super good. Added the al dente ravioli the last 20 mins so as to not overcook. Thanks! Best base recipe and I give you credit!

When I retired and winter hit and I couldn't play golf, I got into cooking and gourmet cooking. My wife wasn't retired yet so II did most of the cooking. It has carried over since she retired. I loved the flavors of this recipe and  I made it almost exactly as it was written. One small change. The store did not have cream cheese with chives so I bought cream cheese and I bought chives. My first bites were great but I noticed how the chicken was shredding (because it was so tender) so I shredded the chicken, on my plate, half way through. I recommend shredding the chicken after it is cooked. So many recipes on this site over promise and under deliver. This one met the expectations of the high rating, and I expect it will be better tomorrow when I have leftovers. I followed the chef's suggestion to put it on top of a bed of rice and that worked well. Here is what I am amazed by. I calculated the total calories by adding up everything that went into the pot, divided it by the servings, and this rich, luscious dish is somewhere between 350 and 450 calories a serving, depending upon how much of the sauce you want to use. Low cal, delicious... my kind of meal.

text:
So I followed the recipe, except a few things... First off, the Italian dressing mix in the store contains wheat, which is gluten, which I cannot have. So, I made my own version of this, which took care of the salt too (common complaint in reviews), as I added NO salt to the recipe. I used thyme, parsley, garlic powder, onion powder, two to three pinches of sugar, a dash of paprika, a dash of ancho chili pepper (for extra kick), oregano, basil, and a few dashes of Mrs. McCormick's Garlic and Herb mixed seasoning. Everything else, such as chive and onion cream cheese, wine, etc, remained the same. Oh and I added a bit of Dubliner's cheese, to make the sauce less sour cream-ish, and more creamy goodness. Yum! I only had 3 chicken breasts, so I froze half the mixture for next time. Will make again!

text:
I loved this recipe.  The sauce is incredible.  Normally I never make changes to a recipe the first time I fix it, but this time I made two changes.  First, it calls for 4 chicken breast halves.  Somewhere they must sell chicken breasts that only weigh 5 to 6 oz each, but not where I live.  I bought 3 chicken breast halves and even that weighed close to 2 1/2 pounds, almost 10 oz per serving.  I fileted them in half lengthwise and got 6 servings, but it tasted so good, I made 5 portions out of it and cut up the 6th and portioned it among the 5.  Second, I like wine in recipes but don't drink it.  I couldn't rationalize buying a bottle of wine to use half a cup and throw out the rest.  I wanted more "on edge" flavor than chicken broth would add, so I substituted apple juice and added a little bit of red wine vinegar to cut some of the sweetness.  I think it worked well.

text:
I find all the recipes using Italian dressing mix are too salty for our taste.  Rather than reducing it, I use no or low sodium broths and soups to balance it out.  This does the trick for us.  I haven't tried this but I was told to mix the dressing mix with a few tablespoons of water - enough to make it a liquid.  Let it sit for 15 min and the salt will dissolve in the water, pour off the liquid and you'll be left with the seasonings.  if you try this, let me know what you think.

I mixed all the ingredients together in a bowl the night before, just microwaved it a minute or so, to make it easier. Then I submerged 2 chicken breasts and poked a few holes in them with a fork, gotta get all that flavor in there too! :) I dumped it in the crockpot at 6am, on low for 5 hours (since my food was cold and the crockpot would need time to heat up) kept it on warm after the 5 hours and by the time I came home from work...ahhhh. This is my husband's favorite! Only things I change: I use chicken broth instead of wine and cream of chicken soup instead of mushroom due to an allergy. text:
I don't know how the initial idea to blend these ingredients came together, but they are beautiful! The Italian seasoning with the Chive and Onion cream cheese is a reward to the palate! I did modify it a little bit, since my wife and kids don't like mushrooms. I used condensed cream of chicken instead of the mushroom and I also wanted to add a little acidity so I added a can of petite diced tomatoes (15 oz Hunts). Also, make sure you taste test the wine while preparing... this is key. :) The tomatoes really gave it a rustic Italian flair! I thought it would be a good fit over pasta, so I felt it wouldn't be enough sauce, so I also added a can of Cream of mushroom soup as well as 1/4 cup of chicken stock. I served over Egg Noodles and the family LOVED IT. I will definitely make again! Thanks a ton!

The dish is wonderful over rice or angel hair pasta.  I also cook it on low for 8 hours- a perfect comfort dish for a busy day!

text:
Wonderfully rich and delicious winter comfy food! Tweaks: used 3.5 lb of boneless, skinless thighs (remove excess fat) instead of breasts (so much flavorful), used  golden mushroom soup &  cream of chicken soup, used Wishbone Parmesan Italian dressing  + cup instead of mix, used wine and chicken stock ( & ) but  found another  cup of wine stirred in before serving, as well as a bit more (1tsp) of butter and 2 Tlsp of horseradish mustard really made it pop. Also added some favorite spices & herbs from Penzey's. Served over brown rice & quinoa, with steamed broccoli & sauce (Italian dressing, mayo & a dash of hot sauce) a glass of your favorite wine (robust red for me) or beverage & some rolls or crusty bread. I would use either the golden mushroom soup or cream of chicken exclusively, not mix them again.

text:
This recipe is a regular in my household ever since I found it a few years ago. I love how easy it is and how few ingredients it takes. I skip the first couple of steps and just throw all the ingredients together in the slow cooker. I cook on high for a few hours and then stir the ingredients all together and serve over egg noodles. I, like other reviewers, substitute condensed low-fat cream of mushroom or cream of chicken soup for the golden mushroom soup. I use regular, reduced fat cream cheese instead of the sour cream and chive. I also sometimes substitute chicken broth for the white wine and sometimes I leave out the extra moisture altogether. This recipe makes the most delicious sauce, even without it.

text:
This was fast and easy, but it didn't knock my socks off.  Like others, I used cream of mushroom soup instead of golden mushroom.  The first time I made it I used 2 lbs of chicken and put it on rice.  It seemed quite salty to me, but I think it's because my sauce to rice ratio was too high.  The next time I used 1 lb or chicken and 1 lb of frozen broccoli and put it on shell pasta.  Much better and not salty when combined with 1 lb of pasta.  Next time I might use a little less pasta, though.  I added the frozen broccoli at an hour before serving like someone else suggested, but I think it was over done.  Maybe half an hour would be better.  I'm sure fresh broccoli cooked with the pasta would be best of all, but then the recipe isn't as fast to make!  I used the standard crock pot time, 6-8 hours on low and it turned out fine (4 hours is usually used for a high setting).  I also cut the chicken breasts into smaller pieces before cooking.
